dollar</a> (<a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">SBD</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Time zone</th><td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>+11</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand traffic">Driving side</a></th><td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">left</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Telephone numbers in Solomon Islands">Calling code</a></th><td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%2B677" title="+677">+677</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:SB" title="ISO 3166-2:SB">SB</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.sb" title=".sb">.sb</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Solomon Islands</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> consisting of six major islands and over 900 smaller islands in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> lying to the east of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> and northwest of <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> and covering a land area of 28,400 square kilometres (11,000&#160;sq&#160;mi). The country\'s capital, <a href="/wiki/Honiara" title="Honiara">Honiara</a>, is located on the island of <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal" title="Guadalcanal">Guadalcanal</a>. The country takes its name from <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_(archipelago)" title="Solomon Islands (archipelago)">the Solomon Islands archipelago</a>, which is a collection of <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesian</a> islands that also includes the <a href="/wiki/North_Solomon_Islands" title="North Solomon Islands">North Solomon Islands</a> (part of Papua New Guinea), but excludes outlying islands, such as <a href="/wiki/Rennell_and_Bellona_Province" title="Rennell and Bellona Province">Rennell and Bellona</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Islands" title="Santa Cruz Islands">Santa Cruz Islands</a>.\n</p><p>The islands have been inhabited for thousands of years. In 1568, the Spanish navigator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_de_Menda%C3%B1a" title="&#193;lvaro de Menda&#241;a">&#193;lvaro de Menda&#241;a</a> was the first European to visit them, naming them the <i>Islas Salom&#243;n</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Princeton_University_Library_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Princeton_University_Library-6">[6]</a></sup> Britain defined its area of interest in the Solomon Islands archipelago in June 1893, when Captain Gibson R.N., of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Curacoa_(1878)" title="HMS Curacoa (1878)">HMS&#160;<i>Curacoa</i></a>, declared the southern Solomon Islands a <a href="/wiki/British_protectorate" title="British protectorate">British protectorate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_campaign" title="Solomon Islands campaign">Solomon Islands campaign</a> (1942&#8211;1945) saw fierce fighting between the United States and the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a>, such as in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guadalcanal" title="Battle of Guadalcanal">Battle of Guadalcanal</a>.\n</p><p>The official name of the then British administration was changed from "the <a href="/wiki/British_Solomon_Islands" title="British Solomon Islands">British Solomon Islands</a> Protectorate" to "the Solomon Islands" in 1975, and self-government was achieved the year after. Independence was obtained in 1978 and the name changed to just "Solomon Islands", without the "the". Today, the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a>   is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Monarchy of Solomon Islands">Queen of Solomon Islands</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, as its <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rick_Houenipwela" title="Rick Houenipwela">Rick Houenipwela</a> is <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Prime Minister of Solomon Islands">the current prime minister</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" tocsection-18"><a href="#Water_and_sanitation"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Water and sanitation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a class="toctext">Energy</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Ethnic_groups"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ethnic groups</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Languages"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Languages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Religion"><span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Media"><span class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Cultural_issues/concerns"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Cultural issues/concerns</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 1568, the Spanish navigator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_de_Menda%C3%B1a" title="&#193;lvaro de Menda&#241;a">&#193;lvaro de Menda&#241;a</a> was the first European to visit the Solomon Islands archipelago, naming it <i>Islas Salom&#243;n</i> ("Solomon Islands") after the wealthy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biblical" title="Biblical">biblical</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Solomon" title="King Solomon">King Solomon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Princeton_University_Library_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Princeton_University_Library-6">[6]</a></sup> It is said that they were given this name in the mistaken assumption that they contained great riches,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> and he believed them to be the Bible-mentioned city of <a href="/wiki/Ophir" title="Ophir">Ophir</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During most of the period of British rule the territory was officially named "the British Solomon Islands Protectorate".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-10">[10]</a></sup> On 22 June 1975 the territory was renamed "the Solomon Islands".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-10">[10]</a></sup> When Solomon Islands became independent in 1978, the name was changed to "Solomon Islands". The definite article, "the", is not part of the country\'s official name but is sometimes used, both within and outside the country.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Solomon_Islands" title="History of Solomon Islands">History of Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Solomon_Islands_canoe_crop.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="485" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Solomon_Islands_canoe_crop.jpg/220px-Solomon_Islands_canoe_crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Solomon_Islands_canoe_crop.jpg/330px-Solomon_Islands_canoe_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Solomon_Islands_canoe_crop.jpg/440px-Solomon_Islands_canoe_crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Solomon_Islands_canoe_crop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Solomon Island warriors, armed with spears, on board an ornamented war canoe (1895).</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>It is believed that <a href="/wiki/East_Papuan_languages" title="East Papuan languages">Papuan</a>-speaking settlers began to arrive around 30,000&#160;BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Austronesia" title="Austronesia">Austronesian</a> speakers arrived c.&#160;4000&#160;BC also bringing cultural elements such as the <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_canoe" title="Outrigger canoe">outrigger canoe</a>. Between 1200 and 800 BC the ancestors of the <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesians</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lapita" title="Lapita">Lapita</a> people, arrived from the <a href="/wiki/Bismarck_Archipelago" title="Bismarck Archipelago">Bismarck Archipelago</a> with their characteristic <a href="/wiki/Ceramic" title="Ceramic">ceramics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="European_contact_.281568.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="European_contact_(1568)">European contact (1568)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: European contact (1568)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German_New_Guinea" title="German New Guinea">German New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Western_Pacific_Territories" title="British Western Pacific Territories">British Western Pacific Territories</a>, and <a href="/wiki/British_Solomon_Islands" title="British Solomon Islands">British Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<p>The first European to visit the islands was the Spanish navigator <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_de_Menda%C3%B1a_de_Neira" title="&#193;lvaro de Menda&#241;a de Neira">&#193;lvaro de Menda&#241;a de Neira</a>, coming from <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">Peru</a> in 1568.\n</p><p>Some of the earliest and most regular foreign visitors to the islands were <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a> vessels from Britain, the United States and Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> They came for food, wood and water from late in the 18th century and, later, took aboard islanders to serve as crewmen on their ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Relations between the islanders and visiting seamen was not always good and sometimes there was violence and bloodshed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Missionaries began visiting the Solomons in the mid-19th century. They made little progress at first, because "<a href="/wiki/Blackbirding" title="Blackbirding">blackbirding</a>" (the often brutal recruitment or kidnapping of labourers for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_plantation" title="Sugar plantation">sugar plantations</a> in <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>) led to <a href="/wiki/List_of_massacres_in_the_Solomon_Islands" title="List of massacres in the Solomon Islands">a series of reprisals and massacres</a>. The evils of the slave trade prompted the United Kingdom to declare a protectorate over the southern Solomons in June 1893.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1898 and 1899, more outlying islands were added to the protectorate; in 1900 the remainder of the archipelago, <a href="/wiki/North_Solomon_Islands" title="North Solomon Islands">an area previously under German jurisdiction</a>, was transferred to British administration, apart from the islands of <a href="/wiki/Buka_Island" title="Buka Island">Buka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville</a>, which remained under German administration as part of <a href="/wiki/German_New_Guinea" title="German New Guinea">German New Guinea</a>. Traditional trade and social intercourse between the western Solomon Islands of Mono and Alu (the Shortlands) and the traditional societies in the south of Bougainville, however, continued without hindrance.\n</p><p>Missionaries settled in the Solomons under the protectorate, converting most of the population to Christianity. In the early 20th century several British and Australian firms began large-scale coconut planting. Economic growth was slow, however, and the islanders benefited little.\n</p><p>Journalist <a href="/wiki/Joe_Melvin" title="Joe Melvin">Joe Melvin</a> visited in 1892, as part of his undercover investigation into blackbirding. In 1908 the islands were visited by <a href="/wiki/Jack_London" title="Jack London">Jack London</a>, who was cruising the Pacific on his boat, the <i>Snark</i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_campaign" title="Solomon Islands campaign">Solomon Islands campaign</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guadalcanal" title="Battle of Guadalcanal">Battle of Guadalcanal</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Enterprise_(CV-6)_under_attack_and_burning_during_the_Battle_of_the_Eastern_Solomons_on_24_August_1942_(NH_97778).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2051" data-file-width="2736" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/USS_Enterprise_%28CV-6%29_under_attack_and_burning_during_the_Battle_of_the_Eastern_Solomons_on_24_August_1942_%28NH_97778%29.jpg/220px-USS_Enterprise_%28CV-6%29_under_attack_and_burning_during_the_Battle_of_the_Eastern_Solomons_on_24_August_1942_%28NH_97778%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/USS_Enterprise_%28CV-6%29_under_attack_and_burning_during_the_Battle_of_the_Eastern_Solomons_on_24_August_1942_%28NH_97778%29.jpg/330px-USS_Enterprise_%28CV-6%29_under_attack_and_burning_during_the_Battle_of_the_Eastern_Solomons_on_24_August_1942_%28NH_97778%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/USS_Enterprise_%28CV-6%29_under_attack_and_burning_during_the_Battle_of_the_Eastern_Solomons_on_24_August_1942_%28NH_97778%29.jpg/440px-USS_Enterprise_%28CV-6%29_under_attack_and_burning_during_the_Battle_of_the_Eastern_Solomons_on_24_August_1942_%28NH_97778%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Enterprise_(CV-6)_under_attack_and_burning_during_the_Battle_of_the_Eastern_Solomons_on_24_August_1942_(NH_97778).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(CV-6)" title="USS Enterprise (CV-6)">USS&#160;<i>Enterprise</i>&#160;(CV-6)</a> under aerial attack during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Eastern_Solomons" title="Battle of the Eastern Solomons">Battle of the Eastern Solomons</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>With the outbreak of the Second World War most planters and traders were evacuated to Australia and most cultivation ceased. Some of the most intense fighting of the war occurred in the Solomons. The most significant of the Allied Forces\' operations against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Imperial" title="Japanese Imperial">Japanese Imperial</a> Forces was launched on 7 August 1942, with simultaneous naval bombardments and amphibious landings on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Islands" title="Florida Islands">Florida Islands</a> at <a href="/wiki/Tulagi" title="Tulagi">Tulagi</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and Red Beach on <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal" title="Guadalcanal">Guadalcanal</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal_Campaign" title="Guadalcanal Campaign">Battle of Guadalcanal</a> became an important and bloody campaign fought in the Pacific War as the Allies began to repulse Japanese expansion. Of strategic importance during the war were the <a href="/wiki/Coastwatchers" title="Coastwatchers">coastwatchers</a> operating in remote locations, often on Japanese held islands, providing early warning and intelligence of Japanese naval, army and aircraft movements during the campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sergeant-Major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacob_Vouza" title="Jacob Vouza">Jacob Vouza</a> was a notable coastwatcher who, after capture, refused to divulge Allied information in spite of interrogation and torture by Japanese Imperial forces. He was awarded a <a href="/wiki/Silver_Star" title="Silver Star">Silver Star</a> Medal by the Americans, which is the United States\' third-highest decoration for valor in combat.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="740" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg/220px-Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg/330px-Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg/440px-Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>American Marines rest during the 1942 <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal_Campaign" title="Guadalcanal Campaign">Guadalcanal Campaign</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Islanders <a href="/wiki/Biuku_Gasa_and_Eroni_Kumana" title="Biuku Gasa and Eroni Kumana">Biuku Gasa and Eroni Kumana</a> were the first to find the shipwrecked <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> and his crew of the <a href="/wiki/Motor_Torpedo_Boat_PT-109" title="Motor Torpedo Boat PT-109">PT-109</a>. They suggested writing a rescue message on a coconut, and delivered the coconut by paddling a dugout canoe. The coconut was later kept on Kennedy\'s desk when he became <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Solomon Islands was one of the major staging areas of the South Pacific and was home to the famous <a href="/wiki/VMA-214" title="VMA-214">VMF-214 "Black Sheep" Squadron</a> commanded by <a href="/wiki/Pappy_Boyington" title="Pappy Boyington">Major Greg "Pappy" Boyington</a>. "The Slot" was a name for <a href="/wiki/New_Georgia_Sound" title="New Georgia Sound">New Georgia Sound</a>, when it was used by the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Express" title="Tokyo Express">Tokyo Express</a> to supply the Japanese garrison on Guadalcanal. Of more than 36,000 Japanese on Guadalcanal, about 26,000 were killed or missing, 9,000 died of disease, and 1,000 were captured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Independence_.281978.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1978)">Independence (1978)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence (1978)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Local councils were established in the 1950s as the islands stabilised from the aftermath of the Second World War. A new constitution was established in 1970 and elections were held, although the constitution was contested and a new one was created in 1974. In 1973 the first oil price shock occurred, and the increased cost of running a colony became apparent to British administrators.\n</p><p>Following the independence of neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> from Australia in 1975, the Solomon Islands gained self-government in 1976. Independence was granted on 7 July 1978. The first Prime Minister was Sir <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kenilorea" title="Peter Kenilorea">Peter Kenilorea</a>, and Solomon Islands retained the Monarchy.\n</p><p>In September 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">Duke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catherine,_Duchess_of_Cambridge" title="Catherine, Duchess of Cambridge">Duchess</a> of Cambridge visited the islands to mark the 60th anniversary of the accession of Queen Elizabeth II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Ethnic_violence_.281998.E2.80.932003.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_violence_(1998&#8211;2003)">Ethnic violence (1998&#8211;2003)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ethnic violence (1998&#8211;2003)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Commonly referred to as <i>the tensions</i> or <i>the ethnic tension</i>, the initial civil unrest was mainly characterised by fighting between the <a href="/wiki/Isatabu_Freedom_Movement" title="Isatabu Freedom Movement">Isatabu Freedom Movement</a> (also known as the Guadalcanal Revolutionary Army) and the <a href="/wiki/Malaita_Eagle_Force" title="Malaita Eagle Force">Malaita Eagle Force</a> (as well as the Marau Eagle Force). (Although much of the conflict was between Guales and Malaitans, Kabutaulaka (2001)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and Dinnen (2002) argue that the \'ethnic conflict\' label is an oversimplification.)\n</p><p>In late 1998, militants on the island of Guadalcanal began a campaign of intimidation and violence towards Malaitan settlers. During the next year, thousands of Malaitans fled back to Malaita or to the capital, Honiara (which, although situated on Guadalcanal, is predominantly populated by Malaitans and Solomon Islanders from other provinces). In 1999, the Malaita Eagle Force (MEF) was established in response.\n</p><p>The reformist government of <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_Ulufa%27alu" title="Bartholomew Ulufa\'alu">Bartholomew Ulufa\'alu</a> struggled to respond to the complexities of this evolving conflict. In late 1999, the government declared a four-month state of emergency. There were also a number of attempts at reconciliation but to no avail. Ulufa\'alu also requested assistance from Australia and New Zealand in 1999 but his appeal was rejected.\n</p><p>In June 2000, Ulufa\'alu was kidnapped by militia members of the MEF who felt that, although he was a Malaitan, he was not doing enough to protect their interests. Ulufa\'alu subsequently resigned in exchange for his release. <a href="/wiki/Manasseh_Sogavare" title="Manasseh Sogavare">Manasseh Sogavare</a>, who had earlier been Finance Minister in Ulufa\'alu\'s government but had subsequently joined the opposition, was elected as Prime Minister by 23&#8211;21 over <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Boseto" title="Leslie Boseto">Rev. Leslie Boseto</a>. However Sogavare\'s election was immediately shrouded in controversy because six MPs (thought to be supporters of Boseto) were unable to attend parliament for the crucial vote (Moore 2004, n.5 on p.&#160;174).\n</p><p>In October 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Townsville_Peace_Agreement" title="Townsville Peace Agreement">Townsville Peace Agreement</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> was signed by the Malaita Eagle Force, elements of the IFM, and the Solomon Islands Government. This was closely followed by the Marau Peace agreement in February 2001, signed by the Marau Eagle Force, the Isatabu Freedom Movement, the Guadalcanal Provincial Government, and the Solomon Islands Government. However, a key Guale militant leader, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Keke" title="Harold Keke">Harold Keke</a>, refused to sign the agreement, causing a split with the Guale groups. Subsequently, Guale signatories to the agreement led by Andrew Te\'e joined with the Malaitan-dominated police to form the \'Joint Operations Force\'. During the next two years the conflict moved to the Weathercoast of Guadalcanal as the Joint Operations unsuccessfully attempted to capture Keke and his group.\n</p><p>New elections in December 2001 brought Sir <a href="/wiki/Allan_Kemakeza" title="Allan Kemakeza">Allan Kemakeza</a> into the Prime Minister\'s chair with the support of his People\'s Alliance Party and the Association of Independent Members. Law and order deteriorated as the nature of the conflict shifted: there was continuing violence on the Weathercoast while militants in Honiara increasingly turned their attention to crime and extortion. The Department of Finance would often be surrounded by armed men when funding was due to arrive. In December 2002, Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Laurie_Chan" title="Laurie Chan">Laurie Chan</a> resigned after being forced at gunpoint to sign a cheque made out to some of the militants. Conflict also broke out in Western Province between locals and Malaitan settlers. Renegade members of the <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Revolutionary_Army" title="Bougainville Revolutionary Army">Bougainville Revolutionary Army</a> (BRA) were invited in as a protection force but ended up causing as much trouble as they prevented.\n</p><p>The prevailing atmosphere of lawlessness, widespread extortion, and ineffective police prompted a formal request by the Solomon Islands Government for outside help. With the country bankrupt and the capital in chaos, the request was unanimously supported in Parliament.\n</p><p>In July 2003, Australian and Pacific Island police and troops arrived in Solomon Islands under the auspices of the Australian-led <a href="/wiki/Regional_Assistance_Mission_to_Solomon_Islands" title="Regional Assistance Mission to Solomon Islands">Regional Assistance Mission to Solomon Islands</a> (RAMSI). A sizeable international security contingent of 2,200 police and troops, led by Australia and New Zealand, and with representatives from about 20 other Pacific nations, began arriving the next month under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Helpem_Fren" title="Operation Helpem Fren">Operation Helpem Fren</a>. Since this time some commentators have considered the country a <a href="/wiki/Failed_state" title="Failed state">failed state</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> However, other academics argue that rather than being a \'failed state\', it is an unformed state: a state that never consolidated even after decades of independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2006, allegations that the newly elected Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Snyder_Rini" title="Snyder Rini">Snyder Rini</a> had used bribes from Chinese businessmen to buy the votes of members of Parliament led to mass rioting in the capital <a href="/wiki/Honiara" title="Honiara">Honiara</a>. A deep underlying resentment against the minority <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Chinese</a> business community led to much of <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">Chinatown</a> in the city being destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-27">[27]</a></sup> Tensions were also increased by the belief that large sums of money were being exported to China. China sent chartered aircraft to evacuate hundreds of Chinese who fled to avoid the riots. Evacuation of Australian and British citizens was on a much smaller scale. Additional Australian, New Zealand and Fijian police and troops were dispatched to try to quell the unrest. Rini eventually resigned before facing a motion of no-confidence in Parliament, and Parliament elected <a href="/wiki/Manasseh_Sogavare" title="Manasseh Sogavare">Manasseh Sogavare</a> as Prime Minister.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes">Earthquakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Earthquakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/2007_Solomon_Islands_earthquake" title="2007 Solomon Islands earthquake">2007 Solomon Islands earthquake</a> and <a href="/wiki/2013_Solomon_Islands_earthquake" title="2013 Solomon Islands earthquake">2013 Solomon Islands earthquake</a></div>\n<p>On 2 April 2007 at 07:39:56 local time (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC%2B11" title="UTC+11">UTC+11</a>) an earthquake with magnitude 8.1 occurred at hypocenter S8.453 E156.957, 349 kilometres (217 miles) northwest of the island\'s capital, <a href="/wiki/Honiara" title="Honiara">Honiara</a> and south-east of the capital of <a href="/wiki/Western_Province_(Solomon_Islands)" title="Western Province (Solomon Islands)">Western Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gizo,_Solomon_Islands" title="Gizo, Solomon Islands">Gizo</a>, at a depth of 10&#160;km (6.2&#160;miles).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> More than 44 aftershocks with magnitude 5.0 or greater occurred up until 22:00:00 UTC, Wednesday, 4 April 2007. A <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a> followed killing at least 52 people, destroying more than 900 homes and leaving thousands of people homeless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Land upthrust extended the shoreline of one island, <a href="/wiki/Ranongga" title="Ranongga">Ranongga</a>, by up to 70 metres (230&#160;ft) exposing many once pristine coral reefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On February 6, 2013, an earthquake with magnitude of 8.0 occurred at epicentre S10.80 E165.11 in the Santa Cruz Islands followed by a tsunami up to 1.5 metres. At least nine people were killed and many houses demolished. The main quake was preceded by a sequence of earthquakes with a magnitude of up to 6.0.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Politics of Solomon Islands">Politics of Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SI_Houses_of_Parliament.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SI_Houses_of_Parliament.jpg/220px-SI_Houses_of_Parliament.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SI_Houses_of_Parliament.jpg/330px-SI_Houses_of_Parliament.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SI_Houses_of_Parliament.jpg/440px-SI_Houses_of_Parliament.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SI_Houses_of_Parliament.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Solomon Islands\' National Parliament building was a gift from the United States.</div></div></div>\n<p>Solomon Islands is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> and has a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> of government. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Monarchy of Solomon Islands">Monarch of Solomon Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>; she is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Governor-General of Solomon Islands">Governor-General</a> who is chosen by the Parliament for a five-year term. There is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> parliament of 50 members, elected for four-year terms. However, Parliament may be dissolved by majority vote of its members before the completion of its term.\n</p><p>Parliamentary representation is based on single-member constituencies. Suffrage is universal for citizens over age 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Solomon_Islands" title="Prime Minister of the Solomon Islands">Prime Minister</a>, who is elected by Parliament and chooses the cabinet. Each ministry is headed by a cabinet member, who is assisted by a <a href="/wiki/Permanent_secretary" title="Permanent secretary">permanent secretary</a>, a career public servant who directs the staff of the ministry.\n</p><p>Solomon Islands governments are characterised by weak political parties (see <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Solomon_Islands" title="List of political parties in Solomon Islands">List of political parties in Solomon Islands</a>) and highly unstable parliamentary coalitions. They are subject to frequent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Votes_of_no_confidence" title="Votes of no confidence">votes of no confidence</a>, leading to frequent changes in government leadership and cabinet appointments.\n</p><p>Land ownership is reserved for Solomon Islanders. The law provides that resident expatriates, such as the Chinese and <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>, may obtain citizenship through naturalisation. Land generally is still held on a family or village basis and may be handed down from mother or father according to local custom. The islanders are reluctant to provide land for nontraditional economic undertakings, and this has resulted in continual disputes over land ownership.\n</p><p>No military forces are maintained by Solomon Islands although a police force of nearly 500 includes a border protection unit. The police also are responsible for fire service, disaster relief, and maritime surveillance. The police force is headed by a commissioner, appointed by the governor-general and responsible to the prime minister. On 27 December 2006, the Solomon Islands Government took steps to prevent the country\'s Australian police chief from returning to the Pacific nation. On 12 January 2007, Australia replaced its top diplomat expelled from Solomon Islands for political interference in a conciliatory move aimed at easing a four-month dispute between the two countries.\n</p><p>On 13 December 2007, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Manasseh_Sogavare" title="Manasseh Sogavare">Manasseh Sogavare</a> was toppled by a vote of no confidence in Parliament,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> following the defection of five ministers to the opposition. It was the first time a prime minister had lost office in this way in Solomon Islands. On 20 December, Parliament elected the opposition\'s candidate (and former Minister for Education) <a href="/wiki/Derek_Sikua" title="Derek Sikua">Derek Sikua</a> as Prime Minister, in a vote of 32 to 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Judiciary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Judiciary of Solomon Islands">Judiciary of Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<p>The Governor General appoints the Chief Justice of the Supreme Court on the advice of the Prime Minister and the Leader of the Opposition. The Governor General appoints the other justices with the advice of a judicial commission. The <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a> (based in the United Kingdom) serves as the highest appellate court.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Category:Articles_contradicting_other_articles" title="Category:Articles contradicting other articles"><span title="This text contradicts material at the article \'Judicial Committee of the Privy Council\'. (February 2018)">contradictory</span></a></i>]</sup> The current Chief Justice is Sir Albert Palmer.\n</p><p>Since March 2014 Justice Edwin Goldsbrough has served as the President of the Court of Appeal for Solomon Islands. Justice Goldsbrough has previously served a five-year term as a Judge of the High Court of Solomon Islands (2006&#8211;2011). Justice Edwin Goldsbrough then served as the Chief Justice of the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCCJ_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCCJ-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Foreign relations of Solomon Islands">Foreign relations of Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<p>Solomon Islands is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">Interpol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Forum" title="Pacific Islands Forum">Pacific Islands Forum</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Commission" title="South Pacific Commission">South Pacific Commission</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ACP_countries" title="ACP countries">African, Caribbean, and Pacific (ACP) countries</a> (ACP) (<a href="/wiki/Lom%C3%A9_Convention" title="Lom&#233; Convention">Lom&#233; Convention</a>).\n</p><p>The political stage of Solomon Islands was influenced by its position regarding <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Taiwan" title="Foreign relations of Taiwan">the Republic of China</a> (ROC) and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_China" title="Foreign relations of China">the People\'s Republic of China</a> (PRC). Solomon Islands gave <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">diplomatic recognition</a> to the Republic of China (Taiwan),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> recognising it as the sole-legitimate government of all of China, thus giving <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> vital votes in the United Nations. Lucrative investments, political funding and preferential loans from both the Republic of China and the People\'s Republic of China have increasingly manipulated the political landscape of the Solomon Islands.\n</p><p>Relations with <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, which had become strained because of an influx of refugees from the <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville</a> rebellion and attacks on the northern islands of Solomon Islands by elements pursuing Bougainvillean rebels, have been repaired. A 1998 peace accord on Bougainville removed the armed threat, and the two nations regularised border operations in a 2004 agreement.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Although the locally recruited <a href="/wiki/British_Solomon_Islands_Protectorate_Defence_Force" title="British Solomon Islands Protectorate Defence Force">British Solomon Islands Protectorate Defence Force</a> was part of <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied Forces</a> taking part in fighting in the Solomons during the Second World War, the country has not had any regular military forces since independence. The various paramilitary elements of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Solomon_Islands_Police_Force" title="Royal Solomon Islands Police Force">Royal Solomon Islands Police Force</a> (RSIPF) were disbanded and disarmed in 2003 following the intervention of the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Assistance_Mission_to_Solomon_Islands" title="Regional Assistance Mission to Solomon Islands">Regional Assistance Mission to Solomon Islands</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RAMSI" title="RAMSI">RAMSI</a>). RAMSI has a small military detachment headed by an Australian commander with responsibilities for assisting the police element of RAMSI in internal and external security. The RSIPF still operates two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_class_patrol_boat" title="Pacific class patrol boat">Pacific class patrol boats</a> (RSIPV <i>Auki</i> and RSIPV <i>Lata</i>), which constitute the de facto navy of Solomon Islands.\n</p><p>In the long term, it is anticipated that the RSIPF will resume the defence role of the country. The police force is headed by a commissioner, appointed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_general" title="Governor general">governor general</a> and responsible to the Minister of Police, National Security &amp; Correctional Services.\n</p><p>The police budget of Solomon Islands has been strained due to a four-year civil war. Following <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Zoe" title="Cyclone Zoe">Cyclone Zoe</a>\'s strike on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Tikopia" title="Tikopia">Tikopia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anuta" title="Anuta">Anuta</a> in December 2002, Australia had to provide the Solomon Islands government with 200,000 Solomon dollars ($50,000 Australian) for fuel and supplies for the patrol boat <i>Lata</i> to sail with relief supplies. (Part of the work of RAMSI includes assisting the Solomon Islands government to stabilise its budget.)\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Provinces of Solomon Islands">Provinces of Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<p>For local government, the country is divided into ten administrative areas, of which nine are provinces administered by elected provincial assemblies and the tenth is the capital Honiara, administered by the Honiara Town Council.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Human rights in Solomon Islands">Human rights in Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<p>There are human rights concerns and issues in regards to education, water, sanitation, women, and persons who identify as lesbian, gay, bisexual, or transgender.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Solomon_Islands" title="LGBT rights in Solomon Islands">Homosexuality</a> is illegal in Solomon Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td href="/wiki/File:East_Rennell-112643.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> declared <a href="/wiki/East_Rennell" title="East Rennell">East Rennell</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 1998.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Solomon_Isles.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="260" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="143"
