class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Solomon_Isles.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of Solomon Islands.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki,_the_capital_of_Malaita._(10702263414).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg/220px-Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg/330px-Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg/440px-Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki,_the_capital_of_Malaita._(10702263414).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Malaita" title="Malaita">Malaita</a> island</div></div></div>\n<p>Solomon Islands is an island nation that lies east of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> and consists of many islands: <a href="/wiki/Choiseul_Island" title="Choiseul Island">Choiseul</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Shortland_Islands" title="Shortland Islands">Shortland Islands</a>; the <a href="/wiki/New_Georgia_Islands" title="New Georgia Islands">New Georgia Islands</a>; <a href="/wiki/Santa_Isabel_Island" title="Santa Isabel Island">Santa Isabel</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Islands" title="Russell Islands">Russell Islands</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nggela" title="Nggela">Nggela</a> (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Islands" title="Florida Islands">Florida Islands</a>); <a href="/wiki/Malaita" title="Malaita">Malaita</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guadalcanal_(Pacific_Ocean_island)" title="Guadalcanal (Pacific Ocean island)">Guadalcanal</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sikaiana" title="Sikaiana">Sikaiana</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maramasike" title="Maramasike">Maramasike</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulawa" title="Ulawa">Ulawa</a>; <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Uki_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Uki Island (page does not exist)">Uki</a>; <a href="/wiki/Makira" title="Makira">Makira</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Cristobal_(Solomon_Islands)" title="San Cristobal (Solomon Islands)">San Cristobal</a>); <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_(Solomon_Islands)" title="Santa Ana (Solomon Islands)">Santa Ana</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rennell_and_Bellona" title="Rennell and Bellona">Rennell and Bellona</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Islands" title="Santa Cruz Islands">Santa Cruz Islands</a> and the remote, tiny outliers, <a href="/wiki/Tikopia" title="Tikopia">Tikopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anuta" title="Anuta">Anuta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatutaka" title="Fatutaka">Fatutaka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Falkie_Atoll" title="Falkie Atoll">Falkie Atoll</a>.\n</p><p>The country\'s islands lie between latitudes <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_south" title="5th parallel south">5&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_south" title="13th parallel south">13&#176;S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/155th_meridian_east" title="155th meridian east">155&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/169th_meridian_east" title="169th meridian east">169&#176;E</a>. The distance between the westernmost and easternmost islands is about 1,500 kilometres (930&#160;mi). The Santa Cruz Islands (of which Tikopia is part) are situated north of <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> and are especially isolated at more than 200 kilometres (120&#160;mi) from the other islands. <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville</a> is geographically part of the Solomon Islands archipelago but politically part of Papua New Guinea. Falkie Atoll, which is closer to Bougainville than to Choiseul, is part of the nation of Solomon Islands.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The islands\' ocean-equatorial climate is extremely humid throughout the year, with a mean temperature of 26.5&#160;&#176;C (79.7&#160;&#176;F) and few extremes of temperature or weather. June through August is the cooler period. Though seasons are not pronounced, the northwesterly winds of November through April bring more frequent rainfall and occasional squalls or cyclones. The annual rainfall is about 3,050 millimetres (120&#160;in).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Solomon Islands <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> is part of two distinct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrestrial_ecoregion" title="Terrestrial ecoregion">terrestrial ecoregions</a>. Most of the islands are part of the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_rain_forests" title="Solomon Islands rain forests">Solomon Islands rain forests</a> ecoregion, which also includes the islands of Bougainville and Buka; these forests have come under pressure from forestry activities. The Santa Cruz Islands are part of the <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu_rain_forests" title="Vanuatu rain forests">Vanuatu rain forests</a> ecoregion, together with the neighbouring archipelago of Vanuatu. Soil quality ranges from extremely rich volcanic (there are <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanoes</a> with varying degrees of activity on some of the larger islands) to relatively infertile limestone. More than 230 varieties of orchids and other tropical flowers brighten the landscape.\n</p><p>The islands contain several active and dormant volcanoes. The Tinakula and <a href="/wiki/Kavachi" title="Kavachi">Kavachi</a> volcanoes are the most active.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_and_sanitation">Water and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Water and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>See also:</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Human rights in Solomon Islands">Human rights in Solomon Islands</a></i>\n</p><p>Scarcity of fresh water sources and lack of sanitation has been a constant challenge facing Solomon Islands. Reducing the number of those living without access to fresh water and sanitation by half was one of the 2015 Millennium Development Goals (MDG\'s) implemented by the United Nations through Goal 7, to ensure environmental sustainability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sectors_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sectors-38">[38]</a></sup> Though the islands generally have access to fresh water sources, it is typically only available in the state\'s capital of Honiara,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sectors_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sectors-38">[38]</a></sup> and it is not guaranteed all year long.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> According to a UNICEF report, even the capital\'s poorest communities do not have access to adequate places to relieve their waste, and an estimated 70% Solomon Island schools have no access to safe and clean water for drinking, washing and relieving of waste.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sectors_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sectors-38">[38]</a></sup> Lack of safe drinking water in school-age children results in high risks of contracting fatal diseases such as cholera and typhoid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb.int_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb.int-40">[40]</a></sup> The number of Solomon Islanders living with piped drinking water has been decreasing since 2011, while those living with non-piped water increased between 2000 and 2010. Nevertheless, one improvement is that those living with non-piped water has been decreasing consistently since 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition, the Solomon Islands Second Rural Development Program, enacted in 2014 and active until 2020, has been working to deliver competent infrastructure and other vital services to rural areas and villages of the Solomon Islands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> which suffer the most from lack of safe drinking water and proper sanitation. Through improved infrastructure, services and resources, the program has also encouraged farmers and other agricultural sectors, through community-driven efforts, to connect them to the market, thus promoting economic growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb.int_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb.int-40">[40]</a></sup> Rural villages such as Bolava, found in the Western Province of Solomon Islands, have benefited greatly from the program, with the implementation of water tanks and rain catchment and water storage systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb.int_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb.int-40">[40]</a></sup> Not only has the improved infrastructure increased the quality of life in Solomon Islands, the services are also operated and developed by the community, thus creating a sense of communal pride and achievement among those previously living in hazardous conditions. The program is funded by various international development actors such as the World Bank, European Union, International Fund for Agricultural Development (IFAD), and the Australian and Solomon Islands governments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb.int_40-3"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb.int-40">[40]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Economy of Solomon Islands">Economy of Solomon Islands</a></div><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">September 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Solomon Islands\' per-capita GDP of $600 ranks it as a lesser developed nation, and more than 75% of its labour force is engaged in subsistence and fishing. Most manufactured goods and petroleum products must be imported. Until 1998, when world prices for tropical timber fell steeply, timber was Solomon Islands\' main export product, and, in recent years, Solomon Islands forests were dangerously <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">overexploited</a>.\n</p><p>Other important cash crops and exports include <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a>. In 1998 gold mining began at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gold_Ridge_(mine)" title="Gold Ridge (mine)">Gold Ridge</a> on Guadalcanal. Minerals exploration in other areas continued. In the wake of the ethnic violence in June 2000, exports of palm oil and gold ceased while exports of timber fell. The islands are rich in undeveloped mineral resources such as lead, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, nickel, and gold.\n</p><p>Solomon Islands\' fisheries also offer prospects for export and domestic economic expansion. A Japanese joint venture, Solomon Taiyo Ltd., which operated the only fish cannery in the country, closed in mid-2000 as a result of the ethnic disturbances. Though the plant has reopened under local management, the export of tuna has not resumed. Negotiations are underway that may lead to the eventual reopening of the Gold Ridge mine and the major oil-palm plantation.\n</p><p>Tourism, particularly diving, is an important service industry for Solomon Islands. Tourism growth is hampered by lack of infrastructure and transportation limitations.\n</p><p>The Solomon Islands Government was insolvent by 2002. Since the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Assistance_Mission_to_Solomon_Islands" title="Regional Assistance Mission to Solomon Islands">RAMSI</a> intervention in 2003, the government has recast its budget. It has consolidated and renegotiated its domestic debt and with Australian backing, is now seeking to renegotiate its foreign obligations. Principal aid donors are Australia, New Zealand, the European Union, Japan, and the Republic of China, Taiwan.\n</p><p>Recently,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> Solomon Islands courts have re-approved the export of live dolphins for profit, most recently to Dubai, United Arab Emirates. This practice was originally stopped by the government in 2004 after international uproar over a shipment of 28 live dolphins to Mexico. The move resulted in criticism from both Australia and New Zealand as well as several conservation organisations.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_dollar" title="Solomon Islands dollar">Solomon Islands dollar</a> (<a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">ISO 4217</a> code: <i>SBD</i>) was introduced in 1977, replacing the Australian Pound Sterling. Its symbol is "SI$", but the "SI" prefix may be omitted if there is no confusion with other currencies also using the <a href="/wiki/Dollar_sign" title="Dollar sign">dollar sign</a> "$". It is subdivided into 100 <a href="/wiki/Cent_(currency)" title="Cent (currency)">cents</a>. Local <a href="/wiki/Shell_money" title="Shell money">shell money</a> is still important for traditional and ceremonial purposes in certain provinces and, in some remote parts of the country, for trade. Shell money was a widely used traditional currency in the Pacific Islands, in Solomon Islands, it is mostly manufactured in <a href="/wiki/Malaita" title="Malaita">Malaita</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal" title="Guadalcanal">Guadalcanal</a> but can be bought elsewhere, such as the <a href="/wiki/Honiara_Central_Market" title="Honiara Central Market">Honiara Central Market</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Barter" title="Barter">barter</a> system often replaces money of any kind in remote areas.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A team of renewable energy developers working for the <a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Applied_Geoscience_Commission" title="South Pacific Applied Geoscience Commission">South Pacific Applied Geoscience Commission</a> (SOPAC) and funded by the <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Energy_and_Energy_Efficiency_Partnership" title="Renewable Energy and Energy Efficiency Partnership">Renewable Energy and Energy Efficiency Partnership</a> (REEEP), have developed a scheme that allows local communities to access renewable energy, such as solar, water and wind power, without the need to raise substantial sums of cash. Under the scheme, islanders who are unable to pay for solar lanterns in cash may pay instead in kind with crops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Demographics of Solomon Islands">Demographics of Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.09\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.4\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.6\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>As of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 599,419&#160;people in Solomon Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_close_up_shot_of_three_junior_AFL_player_holding_footballs_at_the_Lord_Howe_Settlement,_Honiara._(10661462334).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/A_close_up_shot_of_three_junior_AFL_player_holding_footballs_at_the_Lord_Howe_Settlement%2C_Honiara._%2810661462334%29.jpg/220px-A_close_up_shot_of_three_junior_AFL_player_holding_footballs_at_the_Lord_Howe_Settlement%2C_Honiara._%2810661462334%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/A_close_up_shot_of_three_junior_AFL_player_holding_footballs_at_the_Lord_Howe_Settlement%2C_Honiara._%2810661462334%29.jpg/330px-A_close_up_shot_of_three_junior_AFL_player_holding_footballs_at_the_Lord_Howe_Settlement%2C_Honiara._%2810661462334%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/A_close_up_shot_of_three_junior_AFL_player_holding_footballs_at_the_Lord_Howe_Settlement%2C_Honiara._%2810661462334%29.jpg/440px-A_close_up_shot_of_three_junior_AFL_player_holding_footballs_at_the_Lord_Howe_Settlement%2C_Honiara._%2810661462334%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_close_up_shot_of_three_junior_AFL_player_holding_footballs_at_the_Lord_Howe_Settlement,_Honiara._(10661462334).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Solomon Islander boys from Honiara</div></div></div>\n<p>The majority of Solomon Islanders are ethnically <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melanesian" title="Melanesian">Melanesian</a> (94.5%). <a href="/wiki/Polynesians" title="Polynesians">Polynesian</a> (3%) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Micronesian_people" title="Micronesian people">Micronesian</a> (1.2%) are the two other significant groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile:_Solomon_Islands_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile:_Solomon_Islands-45">[45]</a></sup> There are a few thousand ethnic <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Languages of Solomon Islands">Languages of Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<p>While English is the official language, only 1&#8211;2% of the population are able to communicate fluently in English. However, an English creole, Solomons <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pijin" title="Pijin">Pijin</a>, is a <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of the country spoken by the majority of the population, along with local tribal languages. Pijin is closely related to <a href="/wiki/Tok_Pisin" title="Tok Pisin">Tok Pisin</a> spoken in <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>.\n</p><p>The number of local languages listed for Solomon Islands is 74, of which 70 are living languages and 4 are extinct, according to <i>Ethnologue, Languages of the World</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Melanesian_languages" title="Melanesian languages">Melanesian languages</a> (predominantly of the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Solomonic_languages" title="Southeast Solomonic languages">Southeast Solomonic group</a>) are spoken on the central islands.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Polynesian_languages" title="Polynesian languages">Polynesian languages</a> are spoken on <a href="/wiki/Rennell_Island" title="Rennell Island">Rennell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bellona_Island" title="Bellona Island">Bellona</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Tikopia" title="Tikopia">Tikopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anuta" title="Anuta">Anuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fatutaka" title="Fatutaka">Fatutaka</a> to the far east, <a href="/wiki/Sikaiana" title="Sikaiana">Sikaiana</a> to the north east, and Luaniua to the north (<a href="/wiki/Ontong_Java_Atoll" title="Ontong Java Atoll">Ontong Java Atoll</a>, also known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Howe_Atoll" title="Lord Howe Atoll">Lord Howe Atoll</a>). The immigrant population of Gilbertese (<a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">i-Kiribati</a>) speaks a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Micronesian_language" title="Micronesian language">Micronesian language</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Religion in Solomon Islands">Religion in Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<p>The religion of Solomon Islands is mainly Christian (comprising about 92% of the population). The main Christian denominations are: the Anglican <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Province_of_Melanesia" title="Church of the Province of Melanesia">Church of Melanesia</a> 35%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> 19%, <a href="/wiki/South_Seas_Evangelical_Church" title="South Seas Evangelical Church">South Seas Evangelical Church</a> 17%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Church_in_Papua_New_Guinea_and_the_Solomon_Islands" title="United Church in Papua New Guinea and the Solomon Islands">United Church in Papua New Guinea and the Solomon Islands</a> 11% and <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist</a> 10%. Other Christian denominations are <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah\'s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a>, New Apostolic Church (80 churches) and <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (LDS Church).\n</p><p>Another 5% adhere to aboriginal beliefs. The remaining adhere to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baha%27i_Faith" title="Baha\'i Faith">Baha\'i Faith</a>. According to the most recent reports, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islam_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Islam in Solomon Islands">Islam in Solomon Islands</a> is made up of approximately 350 Muslims,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> including members of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya_Muslim_Community" title="Ahmadiyya Muslim Community">Ahmadiyya Muslim Community</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Female life expectancy at birth was at 66.7 years and male life expectancy at birth at 64.9 in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-49">[49]</a></sup> 1990&#8211;1995 fertility rate was at 5.5 births per woman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-49">[49]</a></sup> Government expenditure on health per capita was at US$99 (PPP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-49">[49]</a></sup> Healthy life expectancy at birth is at 60 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_49-3"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-49">[49]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Blond hair occurs in 10% of the population in the islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Loury_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Loury-50">[50]</a></sup> After years of questions, studies have resulted in the better understanding of the blond gene. The findings show that the blond hair trait is due to an amino acid change of protein <a href="/wiki/TYRP1" title="TYRP1">TYRP1</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> This accounts for the highest occurrence of blond hair outside of European influence in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> While 10% of Solomon Islanders display the blond phenotype, about 26% of the population carry the recessive trait for it as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg/220px-Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg/330px-Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg/440px-Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Children at the school in Tuo village, <a href="/wiki/Fenualoa" title="Fenualoa">Fenualoa</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Education in Solomon Islands is not compulsory and only 60 percent of school-age children have access to primary education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spc.int_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-spc.int-55">[55]</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 1990 to 1994, the gross primary school enrolment rose from 84.5 percent to 96.6 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-54">[54]</a></sup> Primary school attendance rates were unavailable for Solomon Islands as of 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-54">[54]</a></sup> While enrolment rates indicate a level of commitment to education, they do not always reflect children\'s participation in school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_54-3"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-54">[54]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Department of Education and Human Resource Development efforts and plans to expand educational facilities and increase enrolment. However, these actions have been hindered by a lack of government funding, misguided teacher training programs, poor co-ordination of programs, and a failure of the government to pay teachers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_54-4"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-54">[54]</a></sup> The percentage of the government\'s budget allocated to education was 9.7 percent in 1998, down from 13.2 percent in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_54-5"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-54">[54]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Male educational attainment tends to be higher than female educational attainment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spc.int_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-spc.int-55">[55]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_University_of_the_South_Pacific" title="The University of the South Pacific">The University of the South Pacific</a> has a Campus at <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal" title="Guadalcanal">Guadalcanal</a> as a foothold in the country while this University has established by Papua New Guinea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Culture of Solomon Islands">Culture of Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malaitan_Chief.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="451" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/24/Malaitan_Chief.jpg/170px-Malaitan_Chief.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/24/Malaitan_Chief.jpg/255px-Malaitan_Chief.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/24/Malaitan_Chief.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Malaitan_Chief.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Malaita" title="Malaita">Malaitan</a> Chief.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Culture of Solomon Islands">culture of Solomon Islands</a> reflects the extent of the differentiation and diversity among the groups living within the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_(archipelago)" title="Solomon Islands (archipelago)">Solomon Islands archipelago</a>, which lies within <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, with the peoples distinguished by island, language, topography, and geography. The cultural area includes the nation state of Solomon Islands and the <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville Island</a>, which is a part of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Solomon Islands includes some <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_culture" title="Polynesian culture">culturally Polynesian</a> societies which lie outside the main region of Polynesian influence, known as the <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_Triangle" title="Polynesian Triangle">Polynesian Triangle</a>. There are seven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polynesian_outliers" title="Polynesian outliers">Polynesian outliers</a> within the Solomon Islands: <a href="/wiki/Anuta" title="Anuta">Anuta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bellona_Island" title="Bellona Island">Bellona</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ontong_Java" title="Ontong Java">Ontong Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rennell_Island" title="Rennell Island">Rennell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikaiana" title="Sikaiana">Sikaiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tikopia" title="Tikopia">Tikopia</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vaeakau-Taumako" title="Vaeakau-Taumako">Vaeakau-Taumako</a>.\n</p><p>In the traditional culture of Solomon Islands, age-old customs are handed down from one generation to the next, allegedly from the ancestral spirits themselves, to form the cultural values of Solomon Islands.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<dl><dt>Radio</dt></dl>\n<p>Radio is the most influential type of media in Solomon Islands due to language differences, illiteracy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and the difficulty of receiving television signals in some parts of the country. The <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Solomon Islands Broadcasting Corporation">Solomon Islands Broadcasting Corporation</a> (SIBC) operates public radio services, including the national stations <i><a href="/wiki/Radio_Happy_Isles" title="Radio Happy Isles">Radio Happy Isles</a></i> 1037 on the dial and <i><a href="/wiki/Wantok_FM" title="Wantok FM">Wantok FM</a></i> 96.3, and the provincial stations <i><a href="/wiki/Radio_Happy_Lagoon" title="Radio Happy Lagoon">Radio Happy Lagoon</a></i> and, formerly, <i>Radio Temotu</i>. There are two commercial FM stations, Z FM at 99.5 in Honiara but receivable over a large majority of island out from Honiara, and, PAOA FM at 97.7 in Honiara (also broadcasting on 107.5 in Auki), and, one community FM radio station, Gold Ridge FM on 88.7.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Newspapers</dt></dl>\n<p>There is one daily newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Solomon_Star" title="Solomon Star">Solomon Star</a></i> and one daily online news website <i>Solomon Times Online (www.solomontimes.com)</i>, two weekly papers <i>Solomons Voice</i> and <i>Solomon Times</i>, and two monthly papers <i>Agrikalsa Nius</i> and the <i>Citizen\'s Press</i>.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Television</dt></dl>\n<p>There are no TV services that cover the entire Solomon Islands, but satellite TV stations can be received. However, in Honiara, there is a free-to-air channel called One Television, and rebroadcast <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_Asia_Pacific" title="ABC Asia Pacific">ABC Asia Pacific</a> (from Australia\'s ABC) and <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_News" title="BBC World News">BBC World News</a>. As of Dec 2010, residents could subscribe to SATSOL, a digital pay TV service, re-transmitting satellite television.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Music of Solomon Islands">Music of Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4073" data-file-width="5310" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg/220px-Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg/330px-Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg/440px-Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A pan flute, nineteenth century, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MHNT" title="MHNT">MHNT</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Melanesia" title="Music of Melanesia">Melanesian music</a> in Solomon Islands includes both group and solo vocals, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slit-drum" title="Slit-drum">slit-drum</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panpipe" title="Panpipe">panpipe</a> ensembles. In the 1920s, bamboo music gained a following. In the 1950s, <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Nanau_Sitori" title="Edwin Nanau Sitori">Edwin Nanau Sitori</a> composed the song "<a href="/wiki/Walkabout_long_Chinatown" title="Walkabout long Chinatown">Walkabout long Chinatown</a>", which has been referred to by the government as the unofficial "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_song" title="National song">national song</a>" of the Solomon Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Modern Solomon Islander popular music includes various kinds of rock and reggae as well as <i>island music</i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_literature" title="Solomon Islands literature">Solomon Islands literature</a></div>\n<p>Writers from Solomon Islands include the novelists <a href="/wiki/Rexford_Orotaloa" title="Rexford Orotaloa">Rexford Orotaloa</a> and John Saunana and the poet Jully Makini.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Sport in Solomon Islands">Sport in Solomon Islands</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Rugby union in Solomon Islands">Rugby union</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_national_rugby_union_team" title="Solomon Islands national rugby union team">Solomon Islands national rugby union team</a> has played internationals since 1969. It took part in the Oceania qualifying tournament for the 2003 and 2007 Rugby World Cups, but did not qualify on either occasion.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_national_football_team" title="Solomon Islands national football team">Solomon Islands national football team</a> has proved among the most successful in Oceania and is part of the OFC confederation in FIFA. They are currently ranked 184th out of 209 teams in the FIFA World Rankings. The team became the first team to beat New Zealand in qualifying for a play-off spot against Australia for qualification to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Cup_2006" title="World Cup 2006">World Cup 2006</a>. They were defeated 7&#8211;0 in Australia and 2&#8211;1 at home.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">Futsal</a>: Closely related to Association Football. On 14 June 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_national_futsal_team" title="Solomon Islands national futsal team">Solomon Islands national futsal team</a>, the Kurukuru, won the Oceania Futsal Championship in Fiji to qualify them for the <a href="/wiki/2008_FIFA_Futsal_World_Cup" title="2008 FIFA Futsal World Cup">2008 FIFA Futsal World Cup</a>, which was held in Brazil from 30 September to 19 October 2008. Solomon Islands is the futsal defending champions in the Oceania region. In 2008 and 2009 the Kurukuru won the Oceania Futsal Championship in Fiji. In 2009 they defeated the host nation <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, 8&#8211;0, to claim the title. The Kurukuru currently hold the world record for the fastest ever goal scored in an official futsal match. It was set by Kurukuru captain Elliot Ragomo, who scored against <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia_national_futsal_team" title="New Caledonia national futsal team">New Caledonia</a> three seconds into the game in July 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> They also, however, hold the less enviable record for the worst defeat in the history of the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Futsal_World_Cup" title="FIFA Futsal World Cup">Futsal World Cup</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> when in 2008 they were beaten by <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_futsal_team" title="Russia national futsal team">Russia</a> with two goals to thirty-one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Beach_soccer" title="Beach soccer">Beach soccer</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_national_beach_soccer_team" title="Solomon Islands national beach soccer team">Solomon Islands national beach soccer team</a>, the Bilikiki Boys, are statistically the most successful team in Oceania. They have won all three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFA_Beach_Soccer_World_Cup_qualification_(OFC)" title="FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup qualification (OFC)">regional championships</a> to date, thereby qualifying on each occasion for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Beach_Soccer_World_Cup" title="FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup">FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup</a>. The Bilikiki Boys are ranked fourteenth in the world as of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, higher than any other team from Oceania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Cultural_issues.2Fconcerns"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_issues/concerns">Cultural issues/concerns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cultural issues/concerns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Solomon Islands has one of the highest rates of family and sexual violence (FSV) in the world with 64% of women aged 15&#8211;49 having reported physical and/or sexual abuse by a partner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ming_2016_16&#8211;19_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ming_2016_16&#8211;19-63">[63]</a></sup> As per a <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) report issued in 2011, "the causes of Gender Based Violence (GBV) are multiple, but it primarily stems from gender inequality and its manifestations."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The report stated: \n</p>\n<dl><dd>"In Solomon Islands, GBV has been largely normalized: 73% of men and 73% of women believe violence against women is justifiable, especially for infidelity and &#8220;disobedience,&#8221; as when women do &#8220;not live up to the gender roles that society imposes.&#8221; For example, women who believed they could occasionally refuse sex were four times more likely to experience GBV from an intimate partner. Men cited acceptability of violence and gender inequality as two main reasons for GBV, and almost all of them reported hitting their female partners as a &#8220;form of discipline,&#8221; suggesting that women could improve the situation by &#8220;[learning] to obey [them].&#8221;</dd></dl>\n<p>Another manifestation and driver of gender inequality in Solomon Islands is the traditional practice of <a href="/wiki/Bride_price#Solomon_Islands" title="Bride price">bride price</a>. Although specific customs vary between communities, paying a bride price is considered similar to a property title, giving men ownership over women. Gender norms of masculinity tend to encourage men to &#8220;control&#8221; their wives, often through violence, while women felt that bride prices prevented them from leaving men." Another report issued by the WHO in 2013 painted a similarly grim picture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, Solomon Islands officially launched the Family Protection Act 2014 aimed at curbing domestic violence in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> While numerous other interventions are being developed and implemented in the healthcare system as well as the criminal justice system, these interventions are still in their infancy and have largely stemmed from Western protocols. Therefore, for these models to be effective, time and commitment is needed to change the cultural perception of domestic violence in Solomon Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ming_2016_16&#8211;19_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ming_2016_16&#8211;19-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul
